       <!--########################### QUICKSTART ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="quickstart"> 
        <div class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Quickstart Guide</h2> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Step 1: Get Your Free API Key</h3> 
          <p><strong>First time users:</strong> If you want to use indico's public API, you must have a free account and API key. To create an account and receive your API key, <a href="/pay-per-call">register here</a>.</p> 
          <p><strong>Returning users:</strong> If you already have an account, you can always retrieve your API key and manage your API usage on your indico dashboard. To access your dashboard, click the login button in the upper right of this screen or go directly to <a href="/dashboard">indico.io/dashboard</a>.</p> 
          <p><strong>Enterprise users:</strong> If you are an enterprise user, you can retrieve your API key and private cloud domain from your indico dashboard. To access your dashboard, click the login button in the upper right of this screen or go directly to <a href="/dashboard">indico.io/dashboard</a>. If you want to become an enterprise user, get <a href="/enterprise">in touch with us</a>, and feel free to play with the public API in the meantime!</p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Step 2: Choose Your Method and Get Started!</h3> 
          <p><strong>Native Support for Multiple Programming Languages:</strong> For your convenience, indico provides native integration with some major programming languages. For installation and usage instructions, click the appropriate link in the left sidebar. Note: We do support Python 3!</p> 
          <p><strong>RESTful API calls:</strong> Don't worry if the programming language you want to use with indico is not listed. You can also use the indico suite of <a href="/product">predictive APIs</a> directly through RESTful API calls. Here is a simple example API call using cURL (you will need to <a href="/pay-per-call">sign up</a> to get your free API key. Replace `YOUR_API_KEY` with your personal API key).</p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <pre class="prettyprint curl always-visible">curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/sentiment' --data '{"data": "indico is so easy to use!"}'</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <!--########################### INSTALL ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="install"> 
        <div id="setup" class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Installation</h2> 
          <p>In order to use the indico APIs, you need a personal API key. If you plan to use one of our client libraries, you'll also need to install a package through a package manager or source.</p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="get_key" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>1. Getting your API key</h3> 
          <p> <strong>First time users:</strong> get a free key by <a href="/pay-per-call">registering for an account</a><br> <strong>Returning users:</strong> check yours by <a href="/dashboard">visiting your dashboard</a><br> <strong>Enterprise users:</strong> check your API key and private cloud domain by <a href="/dashboard">visiting your dashboard</a>, or <a href="/enterprise">contact us</a> if you want to become an enterprise user </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="install_package" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <div ng-show="python"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indicoio</code> PyPi package</h3> 
           <p>There are two methods of installing our Python package.</p> 
           <p> <strong>Method 1 - Installing with <code>pip</code></strong> <br> You can install the latest version of our package using <a href="https://pip.pypa.io/en/stable/">pip</a> </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">pip install indicoio</pre> 
           <p> <strong>Method 2 - Installing from source</strong> <br> You can also install <code>indicoio</code> from source from our <a href="https://github.com/indicodatasolutions/indicoio-python">GitHub repository</a>. </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">git clone https://github.com/IndicoDataSolutions/IndicoIo-Python.git

python setup.py install</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <div ng-show="ruby"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indico</code> RubyGem</h3> 
           <p>There are two methods of installing our Ruby gem</p> 
           <p> <strong>Method 1 - Installing using <code>gem</code></strong> <br> You can install the latest version of the indico RubyGem using <a href="https://rubygems.org/">gem</a> by running the following in your terminal: </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">gem install indico</pre> 
           <p> <strong>Method 2 - Installing using <code>Bundler</code></strong> <br> You can also install indico using Bundler.<br> <br> Add the following to your projects Gemfile: </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">gem indico</pre> 
           <p>Then execute the following terminal command in the project's directory:</p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">bundle install</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <div ng-show="node"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indico.io</code> package</h3> 
           <p>There's one method of installing our node package</p> 
           <p> <strong>Method 1 - Using a package manager</strong> <br> You can install the latest version of our package using <a href="https://www.npmjs.com/">npm</a> </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">npm install indico.io</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <div ng-show="java"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indico</code> package</h3> 
           <p>There are two methods of installing our Java library.</p> 
           <p> <strong>Method 1 - Installing with <code>Maven</code></strong> <br> You can install the latest version of the <code>indico</code> module using <a href="https://search.maven.org/#artifactdetails%7Cio.indico%7Cindico%7C3.X.X%7Cjar">Maven</a> by including the following in your <code>pom.xml</code> file: </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">&lt;dependency&gt;
    &lt;groupId&gt;io.indico&lt;/groupId&gt;
    &lt;artifactId&gt;io.indico&lt;/artifactId&gt;
    &lt;version&gt;3.X.X&lt;/version&gt;
&lt;/dependency&gt;</pre> Be sure to replace the version number with the latest version, which can be found 
           <a href="https://github.com/IndicoDataSolutions/IndicoIo-Java/blob/master/pom.xml">here</a>. 
           <p> <strong>Method 2 - Downloading from Github</strong> <br> All of our client libraries are open source, so if you want the code itself feel free to grab it from github using the command below.<br> </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">git clone https://github.com/IndicoDataSolutions/IndicoIo-Java.git</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <div ng-show="r"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indicoio</code> R wrapper</h3> 
           <p>There's one method of installing our R library</p> 
           <p> <strong>Installing using <code>devtools</code></strong> <br> First, in order for the wrapper to install correctly, you'll need to install biocLite - a third party package manager. This will allow you to install <code>EBImage</code>, an image resizing library that isn't hosted on CRAN (hence the extra step).<br> <br> Then you can install the latest version of the <code>indicoio</code> wrapper using <a href="https://www.rstudio.com/products/rpackages/devtools/">devtools</a>. </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">source("https://bioconductor.org/biocLite.R")
biocLite("EBImage")
</pre> 
           <p> Then you can install the latest version of the <code>indicoio</code> wrapper using <a href="https://www.rstudio.com/products/rpackages/devtools/">devtools</a>. If you don't have <code>devtools</code>, run</p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">install.packages('devtools')</pre> 
           <p>then run</p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">library(devtools)
devtools::install_github("IndicoDataSolutions/IndicoIo-R")</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <div ng-show="php"> 
           <h3>2. Installing the <code>indicoio</code> package</h3> 
           <p>There's one method of installing our PHP package</p> 
           <p> <strong>Installing using <code>Composer</code></strong> <br> You can install the latest version of the <code>indicoio</code> package by following these steps:<br> <br> 1. Create a composer.json file in your project's directory.<br> 2. Write the following in the file: </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">{
  'require': {
    "indicoio/indicoio-php": "*"
  },
  'minimum-stability': "dev"
}</pre> 
           <p> 3. Run the following command in the same directory <strong>(NOTE: You must have composer installed)</strong>: </p> 
           <pre>composer install</pre> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="install_issues" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <!-- PYTHON --> 
         <div ng-show="python"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <hr> 
           <h3>Common installation issues</h3> 
           <p> <strong>Issue 1</strong>: If <code>pip</code> is not recognized as a command, then you may need to install it using <a href="https://pip.pypa.io/en/stable/installing.html#python-os-support">these instructions</a>.<br> <strong>Issue 2</strong>: If you cannot resolve installation issues with your Python distribution, then you can also use <a href="https://store.continuum.io/cshop/anaconda/">Anaconda</a>.<br> <strong>Issue 3</strong>: If installation fails with a <code>TypeError: 'NoneType' object is not callable</code> error, it's likely you're missing the python development headers. On debian based distros, <code>apt-get install python-dev</code> should resolve the issue. <br> <strong>Issue 4</strong>: If installation fails with an error than includes a mention of "jpeg" or "tiff", it's likely your installation of Python's imaging library (Pillow) has failed due to missing dependencies. Please reference <a href="https://pillow.readthedocs.org/en/3.0.x/installation.html">the Pillow install documentation</a> for help with installation. <br> </p> 
           <hr> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example">
           &nbsp;
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- RUBY --> 
         <div ng-show="ruby"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <hr> 
           <h3>Common installation issues</h3> 
           <p> <strong>Issue 1</strong>: If <code>gem</code> is not recognized as a command, then you may need to install it <a href="https://rubygems.org/pages/download">using these instructions</a>.<br> <strong>Issue 2</strong>: If <code>bundle</code> is not recognized as a command, then you may need to install it using the terminal command <code>gem install bundle</code>.<br> </p> 
           <hr> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example">
           &nbsp;
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- NODE --> 
         <div ng-show="node"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <hr> 
           <h3>Common installation issues</h3> 
           <p> <strong>Issue 1</strong>: If <code>npm</code> is not recognized as a command, then you may need to install it using <a href="https://docs.npmjs.com/">these instructions</a>.<br> </p> 
           <hr> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example">
           &nbsp;
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- JAVA --> 
         <div ng-show="java"> 
         </div> 
         <!-- R --> 
         <div ng-show="r"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <hr> 
           <h3>Common installation issues</h3> 
           <p> <strong>Issue 1</strong>: You might require admin rights to install and use <code>devtools</code>, i.e. <code>sudo</code> or <code>run as administrator</code>.<br> <strong>Issue 2</strong>: If you see an error that looks like </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">ERROR: dependency ‘EBImage’ is not available for package ‘indicoio’
* removing ‘/usr/local/lib/R/3.2/site-library/indicoio’</pre> 
           <p> Then you may have also gotten the following error when installing EBImage </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">ERROR: dependency ‘fftwtools’ is not available for package ‘EBImage’
* removing ‘/usr/local/lib/R/3.2/site-library/EBImage’</pre> 
           <p> To fix, you'll need to install fftw tools on your system. For debian-based (ubuntu, etc.) run <code>sudo apt-get install libfftw</code> and for OS X run <code>brew install fftw</code>. Various systems may have different names but searching for <code>[system name] install fftw</code> should get you there. </p> 
           <hr> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example">
           &nbsp;
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <!-- PHP --> 
         <div ng-show="php"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <hr> 
           <h3>Common installation issues</h3> 
           <p> <strong>Issue 1</strong>: If <code>pip</code> is not recognized as a command, then you may need to install it using <a href="https://pip.pypa.io/en/stable/installing.html#python-os-support">these instructions</a>.<br> <strong>Issue 2</strong>: If you cannot resolve installation issues with your Python distribution, then you can also use <a href="https://store.continuum.io/cshop/anaconda/">Anaconda</a>.<br> <strong>Issue 3</strong>: If installation fails with a <code>TypeError: 'NoneType' object is not callable</code> error, it's likely you're missing the python development headers. On debian based distros, <code>apt-get install python-dev</code> should resolve the issue. </p> 
           <hr> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example">
           &nbsp;
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="make_call" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Making your first call!</h3> 
          <p> You should run the following commands in Python to test whether you have successfully installed indicoio. Don't forget, you will need your API key to make your first call. In the code below replace YOUR_API_KEY with your personal API key (the 32-digit alphanumeric sequence assigned to you when you registered with indico). You should get back a number between 0 and 1. </p>

import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.sentiment.predict(
    "I love writing code!"
);
Double result = single.getSentiment();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "I love writing code!",
    "Alexander and the Terrible, Horrible, No Good, Very Bad Day"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.sentiment.predict(example);
List&lt;Double&gt; results = multiple.getSentiment();
System.out.println(results);
</pre>

       <!--########################### CONFIG ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="config"> 
        <div class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Configuration</h2> 
          <p> The indico API supports configuration via several different formats: </p> 
          <ul> 
           <li ng-hide="java">Configuration Files</li> 
           <li ng-show="java">Creating a Properties File</li> 
           <li>Environment Variables</li> 
           <li>Programming Language-specific Syntax</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p> <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> <br> Each of the following configuration methods includes code for specifying a Private Cloud address but this won't apply to you unless you've paid for infrastructure. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="config_file" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div ng-hide="java"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <h3>Configuration File</h3> 
           <p>If you'd like to simply set up your API key once and forget about it, indico supports simple configuration via <code>.indicorc</code> files. This file can either be placed in your home directory or in your current working directory. All settings are optional.</p> 
           <p> <span class="info">Home Directory for Different Systems</span> <br> Linux and OS X:<br> <code>/home/&lt;username&gt;/.indicorc</code> <br><br> Windows:<br> <code>C:\Users\&lt;username&gt;\.indicorc</code> </p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example"> 
           <pre class="prettyprint always-visible">
<span class="nocode com">[auth]</span>
api_key = YOUR_API_KEY

<span class="nocode com">[private_cloud]</span>
cloud = YOUR_PRIVATE_CLOUD</pre> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div ng-show="java"> 
          <div class="method-description"> 
           <h3>Creating a Properties File</h3> 
           <p>This method allows you to store your API key in a configuration file, then reference that file upon object creation. This method allows you to keep your API key out of your code and lets you exercise a little bit more discretion in distributing or open-sourcing any code built on indico.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="method-example"> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">import io.indico.Indico;

String yourApiKey = 'YOUR_API_KEY'
String yourPrivateCloud = 'YOUR_SUBDOMAIN'
Indico indico = new Indico(yourApiKey, yourPrivateCloud);

String filePath = "my/file.properties"
indico.createPropertiesFile(filePath);

// The second indico object is now properly initialized
Indico indicoTwo = new Indico(new File(filePath));
</pre> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="env_var" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Environment Variables</h3> 
          <p ng-hide="java">If you're more comfortable with bash-style configuration, simply setting the <code>$INDICO_API_KEY</code> or <code>$INDICO_CLOUD</code> environment variable is all that is needed to get up and running with the indico API.</p> 
          <p ng-show="java">This method involves setting environment variables, specifically <code>$INDICO_API_KEY</code> and <code>$INDICO_CLOUD</code> (for private cloud users only). The typical method of setting environment variables using the <code>.bashrc</code> don't apply to java given the typical environment set up. For details on setting environment variables in eclipse look at <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/questions/7048216/environment-variables-in-eclipse">this StackOverflow question</a></p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <pre ng-hide="java" class="prettyprint always-visible"># unix
<span class="nocode">export INDICO_API_KEY = YOUR_API_KEY
export INDICO_CLOUD = YOUR_SUBDOMAIN</span>

# windows

<span class="nocode">setx INDICO_API_KEY YOUR_API_KEY
setx INDICO_CLOUD YOUR_SUBDOMAIN</span></pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="lang_specific" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Programming Language-specific syntax</h3> 
          <p><strong>Passing as a function argument</strong> <br>In addition to the methods above, our client libraries each support passing in settings as function arguments. See the code on the right for details.</p> 
          <p ng-hide="r"><strong>Using a module variable</strong> <br>This method allows you to specify your API key a single time within a program or once per interpreter session by defining the module variable. This method eliminates the need to specify your API key or private cloud address more than one time and can help keep your code more readable.</p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
import indicoio

# option 1: pass configuration as a function argument
print(indicoio.sentiment('indico is so easy to use!', api_key="YOUR_API_KEY", cloud="YOUR_SUBDOMAIN"))

# option 2: set module variable
indicoio.config.api_key = 'YOUR_API_KEY'
indicoio.config.cloud = 'YOUR_SUBDOMAIN'
print(indicoio.sentiment('indico is so easy to use!'))

# 0.9782025594088044</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
require 'indico'

# option 1: pass configuration as a function argument
config = {api_key: "YOUR_API_KEY", cloud: "YOUR_SUBDOMAIN"}
puts(Indico.sentiment("indico is so easy to use!", config))

# option 2: set module variable
Indico.api_key = "YOUR_API_KEY"
Indico.private_cloud = "YOUR_SUBDOMAIN"
puts(Indico.sentiment("indico is so easy to use!"))

# {"Sentiment"=&gt;0.9782025594088044}</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
var indico = require('indico.io');

# option 1: pass configuration as a function argument
var settings = {"api_key": "YOUR_API_KEY"};
var results = indico.sentiment('indico is so easy to use!', settings)

# option 2: set module variable
indico.apiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY";
var results = indico.sentiment('indico is so easy to use!')

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

results.then(response).catch(logError);
// 0.9782025594088044</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;

# option 1: pass to instantiation
String yourApiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY"
String yourPrivateCloud = "YOUR_SUBDOMAIN"
Indico indico = new Indico(yourApiKey, yourPrivateCloud);

# option 2: loading from a properties file (see above for making the file)
String filePath = "my/file.properties"
Indico indico = new Indico(new File(filePath));

IndicoResult results = indico.sentiment.predict("indico is so easy to use!");
Double sentiment = results.getSentiment();

System.out.println(sentiment);
// 0.9782025594088044</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
library(indicoio)

# pass configuration as function arguments

# 0.9782025594088044</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">

         </div> 
        </div>

       <!--########################### BATCH ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="batch"> 
        <div class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Batch Requests</h2> 
          <p> Each indicoio function can be called with a batch of data for analyzing many examples with a single network request. This can improve the speed of using the indico APIs significantly. Simply pass in a list of inputs and receive a list of results in return. The optimal balance between the size of the batch requests and the amount of network requests varies case by case, but perfomance is usually optimal between 20-100 examples.<br> <br> <span class="info">Not using the latest package?</span> <br> If you're using an older version of our client libraries the syntax for batch calls is different. Namely, you'll need to call a separate batch function as shown to the right. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
import indicoio
indicoio.config.api_key = 'YOUR_API_KEY'

# Version &gt;= 0.9.0
indicoio.sentiment(['indico is so easy to use!', 'Still really easy, yiss'])

# Version &lt; 0.9.0
indicoio.batch_sentiment(['indico is so easy to use!', 'Still really easy, yiss'])
# [0.9782025594088044, 0.9895808115135271]</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
require 'indico'
config = {api_key: "YOUR_API_KEY"}

# Version &gt; v0.4.0
Indico.sentiment(["indico is so easy to use!", "Still really easy, yiss"], config)
# [0.9782025594088044, 0.9895808115135271]

# Version &lt;= v0.4.0
Indico.batch_sentiment(["indico is so easy to use!", "Still really easy, yiss"], config)
# [0.9782025594088044, 0.9895808115135271]</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
var indico = require('indico.io');

var settings = {"api_key": "YOUR_API_KEY"};
var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

indico.sentiment(['indico is so easy to use!', 'Still really easy, yiss'], settings)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// [0.9782025594088044, 0.9895808115135271]</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;

Indico indico = new Indico("
           <your_api_key>
            ");
List&lt;String&gt; examples = new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;();
examples.add("indico is so easy to use!");
examples.add("Still really easy, yiss");

// Version &gt;= 3.1.0
List&lt;Double&gt; results = test.sentiment.predict(examples).getSentiment();

// Version &lt; 3.1.0
IndicoResult results = indico.batchSentiment.predict(examples).getSentiment();
Double sentiment = results.getSentiment();

// [0.9782025594088044, 0.9895808115135271]
           </your_api_key></pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">

          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">

       <!--########################### BATCH ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="calls"> 
        <div class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Call Usage</h2> 
          <p>For the most part, every article of text or image you send to indico will count as one call towards your monthly call volume. Take note than an "article of text" could be a word, sentence, or entire document. So, if you sent the API a sentence (as a single example) for analysis, then sent the API an entire document (as a single example), you would have made two API calls.</p> 
          <p>Here's some more clarification on how call usage works, as well as a few exceptions:</p> 
          <br> 
          <p><strong>Batch Requests</strong> <br> When you send a batch query to indico, each article of text or image in the query will count as a call. For example, if you query sentiment with a list of 100 text examples, this will be recorded as 100 calls.</p> 
          <p><strong>Analyze Text, Analyze Image, and Intersections</strong> <br> Requests to APIs that query multiple other APIs - <a href="#analyze_text">Analyze Text</a>, <a href="#intersections">Intersections</a>, and <a href="#analyze_image">Analyze Image</a> - count as a call to each API being queried. For example, a non-batch query to Analyze Text where APIs=['sentiment', 'emotion'] will be recorded as two calls.</p> 
          <p><strong>Custom Collections</strong> <br> Custom Collections follows non standard rules for recording calls towards your monthly call volume. If you are using a <a href="#custom">Custom Collection</a>, please check the documentation of the methods you are using to learn how calls are calculated for them.</p> 
          <p><strong>indico Toolkit</strong> <br> All calls to the <a href="/dashboard/analyze">indico Toolkit</a> follow the same rules as any other queries to our APIs and will count towards your monthly call limit.</p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example">
          &nbsp;
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <!--########################### TEXT ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="text"> 
        <div class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Text Analysis</h2> 
          <p> Use our models to analyze text in a variety of contexts! </p> 
          <div class="function-list"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#sentiment"><span ng-bind-html="sentiment"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#sentiment_hq"><span ng-bind-html="sentiment_hq"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#text_tags"><span ng-bind-html="text_tags"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#language"><span ng-bind-html="language"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#political"><span ng-bind-html="political"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#keywords"><span ng-bind-html="keywords"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#people"><span ng-bind-html="people"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#places"><span ng-bind-html="places"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#organizations"><span ng-bind-html="organizations"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#twitter_engagement"><span ng-bind-html="twitter_engagement"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#personality"><span ng-bind-html="personality"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#relevance"><span ng-bind-html="relevance"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#text_features"><span ng-bind-html="text_features"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#emotion"><span ng-bind-html="emotion"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#intersections"><span ng-bind-html="intersections"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#analyze_text"><span ng-bind-html="analyze_text"></span></a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <p class="thumbprint-args"> <br> <b ng-bind-html="data"></b> :<code>String</code> or <code>List</code>: required: The API processes strings as a single piece of text and return a single result. You can also send a list of phrases to be processed all in one call(more efficient).<br> <span ng-show="java"><b ng-bind-html="params"></b> :<code>Map</code>: optional: Some of the functions have optional parameters that are passed to the function with a map, the keys being the names of the options shown below.<br><br></span> <span ng-show="php"><b ng-bind-html="config"></b> :<code>Array</code>: optional: Some of the functions have optional parameters that are passed to the function with an array, the keys being the names of the options shown below.<br><br></span> <b ng-bind-html="api_key"></b> :<code>String</code>: required/optional: Your API key for authenticating your usage. If you haven't set your API key in <a href="#config">another way</a>, this is required.<br> <b ng-bind-html="cloud"></b> :<code>String</code>: optional: If specified, calls will be made to the private cloud address provided. If you haven't purchased private infrastructure from us then this input is irrelevant.<br> <b ng-bind-html="apis"></b> :<code>List</code>: required: For <b>analyze_text</b>, <b>analyze_image</b> and <b>intersections</b> you must provide a list of APIs you'd like to use. <b>intersectiosn</b> requires exactly 2 at a time.<br> <b ng-bind-html="top_n"></b> :<code>Integer</code>: optional: For <b>text tags</b> and <b>keywords</b> we provide the option to get results in order of score up to the specified Nth highest score.<br> <b ng-bind-html="threshold"></b> :<code>Float</code>: optional: Set a threshold that scores must be greater than in order to be returned in the call's response. Currently for <b>text tags</b> and <b>keywords</b>.<br> <b ng-bind-html="independent"></b> :<code>Boolean</code>: optional: For <b>text tags</b> this argument specifies that you'd like each individual probability to be normalized between 0 and 1 rather than the sum of all tag scores adding to 1.<br> <b ng-bind-html="relative"></b> :<code>Boolean</code>: optional: The opposite of {{ independent }}. The <b>keywords</b> API returns independent scores by default and this argument allows you to normalize them such that all scores add to 1.<br> </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint">// These are standard imports that
// are generally handled by your IDE,
// but just to be explicit:
import java.nio.file.Paths;
import java.util.ArrayList;
import java.util.Arrays;
import java.util.Collections;
import java.util.HashMap;

        <div id="text-format" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Input Text Format</h2> 
          <p>Text can be sent to the <code>indicoio</code> text analysis functions as raw text strings or URLs. If the <code>indicoio</code> API detects the text input is a URL, the text function will be run on the webpage text of the URL. Both single and batch requests of over 5 MB will be rejected. Sample code for passing in raw text or a URL is provided below.</p> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <div ng-show="python"> 
           <p><strong>Passing in Raw Text</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">import indicoio

indicoio.sentiment('text to analyze')</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Text URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">import indicoio

indicoio.sentiment('https://TEXT_URL')</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <div ng-show="ruby"> 
           <p><strong>Passing in Raw Text</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">require 'indico'

Indico.sentiment("text to analyze")</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Text URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">require 'indico'

url = "https://TEXT_URL"
Indico.sentiment(url)</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <div ng-show="node"> 
           <p><strong>Passing in Raw Text</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">var indico = require('indico.io')
indico.apiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY";

indico.sentiment("text to analyze")
  .then(function(res) {
    console.log(res);
  }).catch(function(err) {
    console.warn(err);
  });</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Text URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">var indico = require('indico.io')
indico.apiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY";

indico.sentiment("https://TEXT_URL")
  .then(function(res) {
    console.log(res);
  }).catch(function(err) {
    console.warn(err);
  });</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <div ng-show="java"> 
           <p><strong>Sending text through the API</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">import java.io.File;
import java.util.List;
import java.util.Map;
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.text.Sentiment;

Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");

// As a String
IndicoResult responseOne = indico.sentiment.predict("text to analyze");
Double result = responseOne.getSentiment();
System.out.println(result);

// From a URL
IndicoResult responseTwo = indico.sentiment.predict("https://IMAGE_URL");
result = responseTwo.getSentiment();
System.out.println(result);
</pre>

        <div id="sentiment" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Sentiment Analysis</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="sentiment"></strong> <br>Quickly and efficiently determine if text is positive or negative. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/sentiment/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="language_param"></span> - String (defaults to 'english') - optional - The language of the input text. If set to 'detect', Sentiment will first attempt to determine the language of the input text and calculate sentiment in that language. The language options are 'arabic', 'chinese', 'dutch', 'english', 'french', 'german', 'italian', 'japanese', 'korean', 'portuguese', 'russian', and 'spanish'. </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p>This function will return a number between 0 and 1. This number is a probability representing the likelihood that the analyzed text is positive or negative. Values greater than 0.5 indicate positive sentiment, while values less than 0.5 indicate negative sentiment.</p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
0.9819219949985644

# batch output
[
    0.9819219949985644,
    0.00015202198176385973
]
</pre>

Indico.api_key =  'YOUR_API_KEY'

          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
var indico = require('indico.io');
indico.apiKey =  'YOUR_API_KEY';

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

// single example
indico.sentiment("I love writing code!")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "I love writing code!",
    "Alexander and the Terrible, Horrible, No Good, Very Bad Day"
];
indico.sentiment(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.sentiment.predict(
    "I love writing code!"
);
Double result = single.getSentiment();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "I love writing code!",
    "Alexander and the Terrible, Horrible, No Good, Very Bad Day"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.sentiment.predict(example);
List&lt;Double&gt; results = multiple.getSentiment();
System.out.println(results);
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">

)

# batch example
sentiment(
    c(

        "Alexander and the Terrible, Horrible, No Good, Very Bad Day"
    ),
    api_key = 'YOUR_API_KEY'
)

        <div id="sentiment_hq" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>High Quality Sentiment Analysis</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="sentiment_hq"></strong> <br>Highly accurate sentiment analysis but less performant than the standard Sentiment API. Note: Sentiment HQ only supports English analysis. For multilingual support, please use the standard Sentiment API. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/sentimenthq/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p>This function will return a number between 0 and 1. This number is a probability representing the likelihood that the analyzed text is positive or negative. Values greater than 0.5 indicate positive sentiment, while values less than 0.5 indicate negative sentiment.</p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
0.9819219949985644

# batch output
[
    0.9819219949985644,
    0.00015202198176385973
]
</pre>

          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">

        <div id="text_tags" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Text Tags</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="text_tags"></strong> <br>Determine the topics in the phrase or document `str`. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/texttags/[batch]/?version=[version]</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> <span ng-bind-html="version"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 1) - specify model version<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optionals - only return this many of the most likely topics<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float (defaults to 0.) - optional - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-bind-html="independent"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when False, the probabilities of all topics sum to 1, when True, topic probabilities are independent and are not constrained to sum to 1.<br><br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with 111 key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that the analyzed text is about each of the 111 possible topics. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the topic names and the values are the probabilities that the analyzed text is about each topic.<br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
{
    'anime': 0.003982535730280216,
    'anthropology': 0.020311181569223534,
    'archery': 0.4893124752591462,
    ... 105 topics omitted ...,
    'wrestling': 0.0009661379304299885,
    'writing': 0.00532591437084736,
    'yoga': 0.001874647791589776
}

# single example

    "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.",
    "Yoga in Indian traditions, however, is more than physical exercise, it has a meditative and spiritual core."

          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
var indico = require('indico.io');
indico.apiKey =  'YOUR_API_KEY';

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

// single example
indico.textTags("The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.",
    "Yoga in Indian traditions, however, is more than physical exercise, it has a meditative and spiritual core."
];

indico.textTags(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.text.TextTag;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;
import java.util.HashMap;

Map params = new HashMap
           <string, object>
            ();
params.put("threshold", 0.1)

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.textTags.predict(
    "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.", params
);
Map&lt;TextTag, Double&gt; result = single.getTextTags();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.",
    "Yoga in Indian traditions, however, is more than physical exercise, it has a meditative and spiritual core."
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.textTags.predict(example, params);
List&lt;Map&lt;TextTag, Double&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getTextTags();
System.out.println(results);

           </string,></pre>

          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// single example
$.post(
  'https://apiv2.indico.io/texttags',
  JSON.stringify({
    'api_key': "YOUR_API_KEY",
    'data': "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.",
    'threshold': 0.1
  })
).then(function(res) { console.log(res) });

// batch example
$.post(
  'https://apiv2.indico.io/texttags/batch',
  JSON.stringify({
    'api_key': "YOUR_API_KEY",
    'data': [
      "The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.",
      "Yoga in Indian traditions, however, is more than physical exercise, it has a meditative and spiritual core."
    ],
    'threshold': 0.1
  })
).then(function(res) { console.log(res) });

          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# single example
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/texttags' --data '{"data":"The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.", "threshold": 0.1}'

# batch example
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/texttags/batch' --data '{"data":["The most common form of arrow consists of a shaft with an arrowhead attached to the front end and with fletchings and a nock attached to the other end.", "Yoga in Indian traditions, however, is more than physical exercise, it has a meditative and spiritual core."], "threshold": 0.1}'

         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="language" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Language Detection</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="language"></strong> <br>Automatically determine the language of a phrase or document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/language/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 3) - only return this many of the most likely languages<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float - optional (defaults to .0) - only return languages with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-bind-html="independent"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when False, the probabilities of all languages sum to 1, when True, language probabilities are independent and are not constrained to sum to 1.<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with 33 key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that the analyzed text is written in each of the 33 possible languages. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the language names and the values are the probabilities that the analyzed text is written in each language. <br> Values less than 0.05 indicate that it is very unlikely the text is written in the corresponding language. </p> 
          <p> Complete List of Languages: <br> Arabic (ar), Bulgarian (bg), Chinese (ch), Czech (cs), Danish (da), Dutch (nl), English (en), Esparanto (eo), Farsi (fa), Finnish (fi), French (fr), German (de), Greek (el), Hebrew (he), Hungarian (hu), Indonesian (id), Italian (it), Japanese (ja), Korean (ko), Latin (la), Lithuanian (lt), Norwegian (no), Polish (pl), Portuguese (pg), Romanian (ro), Russian (ru), Slovak (sk), Spanish (es), Swedish (sv), Tagalog (tl), Thai (th), Turkish (tr), Vietnamese (vi) </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message -->

        <div id="political" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Political Analysis</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="political"></strong> <br>Gauge the political leanings of a phrase or document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/political/[batch]/?version=[version]</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> <span ng-bind-html="version"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 1) - specify model version, versions 1 and 2 are available<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 3) - only return this many of the most likely topics<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float - optional (defaults to .0) - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number <span ng-bind-html="independent"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when False, the probabilities of all languages sum to 1, when True, language probabilities are independent and are not constrained to sum to 1.<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with 4 key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that each of 4 political leanings are expressed in the analyzed text. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the political leanings and the values are the probabilities that the analyzed text is expressing each political view.<br> <br> Values less than 0.05 indicate that it is very unlikely the text is expressing that particular political leaning. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message -->

import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.text.PoliticalClass;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;
import java.util.HashMap;

Map params = new HashMap
           <string, object>
            ();
params.put("threshold", 0.25)

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.political.predict(
    "I have a constitutional right to bear arms!", params
);
Map&lt;PoliticalClass, Double&gt; result = single.getPolitical();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "I have a constitutional right to bear arms!",
    "I wish more candidates cared about the environment."
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.political.predict(example, params);
List&lt;Map&lt;PoliticalClass, Double&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getPolitical();
System.out.println(results);

        <div id="keywords" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Keywords</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="keywords"></strong> <br>Identify the important words within a document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/keywords/[batch]/?version=[version]</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> <span ng-bind-html="version"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 1) - specify model version<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 3) - only return this many of the most likely topics<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float - optional (defaults to .0) - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-bind-html="relative"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, it will scale the scores for each keyword such that the lowest is 0 and the highest is 1, which makes setting a threshold easier<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the righthand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with top_n key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that each of the extracted keywords are relevant to the analyzed text. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the extracted keywords, and the values are the likelihoods that these keywords are relevant to the analyzed text.<br><br> <b>NOTE:</b> We've deployed a new, more accurate version of keywords that can be accessed by setting the version option to 2. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">

    'state': 0.38810469246709006,
    'sunshine': 0.61189530753291
}

# batch output

    {
        'state': 0.38810469246709006,
        'sunshine': 0.61189530753291
    }, 
    {
        'state': 0.38810469246709006,
        'sunshine': 0.61189530753291
    }
]
</pre>

import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

Map&lt;String, Object&gt; params = new HashMap&lt;String, Object&gt;() {­{
    put("version", 2);
}­};

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.keywords.predict(
    "Some call it the sunshine state",
    params
);
Map&lt;String, Double&gt; result = single.getKeywords();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "Some call it the sunshine state",
    "Some call it the sunshine state"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.keywords.predict(example, params);
List&lt;Map&lt;String, Double&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getKeywords();
System.out.println(results);

        <div id="people" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>People</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="people"></strong> <br>Identify references to specific persons found in a document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/people/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float (defaults to 0.01) - optional - only return named entities with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a list of dictionaries of three key-value pairs. Each dictionary represents a substring from the input document that the model has predicted is a person with confidence greater than your threshold. Eash dictionary has three keys: <code>text</code>, <code>confidence</code>, and <code>position</code>. The <code>text</code> key maps to a substring from the document that is predicted to be a person. The <code>confidence</code> key maps to a float between 0 and 1, representing how confident the model is that the <code>text</code> is a person. The <code>position</code> key maps to a two element list with the start character position and end character position of <code>text</code> in the input document. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">

        'text': 'Mike Brown',
        'confidence':  0.913224,
        'position':  [26, 36]
    }
]

# batch output

    [
        {
            'text': 'Mike Brown',
            'confidence':  0.913224,
            'position':  [26, 36]
        }
    ],
    [

            'text': 'Mike Brown',
            'confidence':  0.913224,
            'position':  [26, 36]
        }
    ]
]

        <div id="places" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Places</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="places"></strong> <br>Identify references to specific places found in a document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/places/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float (defaults to 0.01) - optional - only return named entities with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a list of dictionaries of three key-value pairs. Each dictionary represents a substring from the input document that the model has predicted is a place, with confidence greater than your threshold. Eash dictionary has three keys: <code>text</code>, <code>confidence</code>, and <code>position</code>. The <code>text</code> key maps to a substring from the document that is predicted to be a place. The <code>confidence</code> key maps to a float between 0 and 1, representing how confident the model is that the <code>text</code> is a place. The <code>position</code> key maps to a two element list with the start character position and end character position of <code>text</code> in the input document. </p>

indico.apiKey =  'YOUR_API_KEY';

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

// single example
indico.places("London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ...")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ...",
    "London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ..."
];
indico.places(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;
import java.util.HashMap;

Map params = new HashMap
           <string, object>
            ();
params.put("threshold", 0.01)

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.places.predict(
    "London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ...", params
);
List&lt;Map&lt;String, Object&gt;&gt; result = single.getPlaces();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ...",
    "London Underground's boss Mike Brown warned that the strike ..."
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.places.predict(example, params);
List&lt;List&lt;Map&lt;String, Object&gt;&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getPlaces();
System.out.println(results);

        <div id="organizations" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Organizations</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="organizations"></strong> <br>Identify references to specific organizations found in a document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/organizations/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float (defaults to 0.01) - optional - only return named entities with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a list of dictionaries of three key-value pairs. Each dictionary represents a substring from the input document that the model has predicted is an organization, with confidence greater than your threshold. Eash dictionary has three keys: <code>text</code>, <code>confidence</code>, and <code>position</code>. The <code>text</code> key maps to a substring from the document that is predicted to be an organization. The <code>confidence</code> key maps to a float between 0 and 1, representing how confident the model is that the <code>text</code> is an organization. The <code>position</code> key maps to a two element list with the start character position and end character position of <code>text</code> in the input document. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
[
    {
        'text': 'London Underground',
        'confidence':  0.913224,
        'position':  [0, 18]
    }
]

# batch output
[
    [
        {
            'text': 'London Underground',
            'confidence':  0.913224,
            'position':  [0, 18]
        }
    ],
    [
        {
            'text': 'London Underground',
            'confidence':  0.913224,
            'position':  [0, 18]
        }
    ]
]
</pre>

        <div id="twitter_engagement" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Twitter Engagement</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="twitter_engagement"></strong> <br>Predict audience engagement for a given tweet. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/twitterengagement/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a number between 0 and 1. This number is a probability representing the confidence that the analyzed text will be retweeted or favorited. Values greater than 0.5 indicate high engagement content, while values less than 0.5 indicate low engagement content. </p>

);

        <div id="personality" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Personality</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="personality"></strong> <br>Predicts the personality traits of a text's author. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/personality/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function returns a dictionary that maps the following personality traits to their likelihood of describing the author: extraversion, openness, agreeableness, conscientiousness. These values are independent, meaning the probabilities don't effect each other. For example, somebody could score 0.9 (90%) on extraversion and 0.86 (86%) on openness.<br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
{
    'extraversion': 0.384...,

System.out.println(results);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    I love my friends., 
    I love my friends.
};
List&lt;Map&lt;Personality, Double&gt;&gt; batchResults = indico.personality.predict(example).getPersonality();

        <div id="personas" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Personas</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="persona"></strong> <br>Predicts the Myers Briggs persona of an author based on a sample of text. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/personality/[batch]/?persona=true</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 3) - only return this many of the most likely topics<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float - optional (defaults to .0) - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function returns a dictionary that maps from the <a href="https://www.16personalities.com/personality-types">16 Myers Briggs personas</a> to the probability that the author aligns with the respective persona. <br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON -->

           <string, object>
            ();

// single example

System.out.println(results);

// batch example

    "I only stay home on Saturday nights to read.",
    "I just want to support my friends and always be there for them."
};

        <div id="relevance" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Relevance</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="relevance"></strong> <br>Determine how relevant query terms and phrases are to a given document. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/relevance/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-bind-html="queries"></span> - String | List - required - a list of queries to run against the document<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function returns a list of floating point values representing the relevance of a given search query to the provided document or documents. The <code>`data`</code> argument and the <code>`queries`</code> argument may be either a single text string or a list of text strings. <br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
[0.6740826540660497, 0.16670130847921036]

# batch output
[
    [0.16670130847921036], 
    [0.2949661163493879]
]
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# single output
[0.6740826540660497, 0.16670130847921036]

# batch output
[
    [0.16670130847921036], 
    [0.2949661163493879]
]
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// single output
[0.6740826540660497, 0.16670130847921036]

// batch output
[
    [0.16670130847921036],
    [0.2949661163493879]

    "Renowned soccer legend Pele will be visiting...", 
    "The Queen of England will be visiting..."

String[] queries = {
  "royalty"

        <div id="emotion" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Emotion</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="emotion"></strong> <br>Predicts the emotion expressed by an author in a sample of text. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/emotion/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional (defaults to 3) - only return this many of the most likely topics<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float - optional (defaults to .0) - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number <br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function returns a dictionary that maps from 5 emotions (anger, fear, joy, sadness, surprise) to the probability that the author is expressing the respective emotion. <br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 5 keys, 5 values, and an omitted message -->

        <div id="text_features" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Text Features</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="text_features"></strong> <br>Convert text into meaningful feature vectors.<br> Extracts abstract text features for use as inputs to learning algorithms. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/textfeatures/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> List of 300 numbers (floats). Each number corresponds to the strength of that feature in the feature vector. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">

    0.003421281571050769,
    ... 294 features omitted ...,
    -0.0599560840072811,
    0.07137194953658677,
    -0.008098228765861361
]

var indico = require('indico.io');
indico.apiKey =  'YOUR_API_KEY';

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

// single example
indico.textFeatures("There are so many things you can learn from text.")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "There are so many things you can learn from text.",
    "You could use the features to train a model!"
];
indico.textFeatures(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.text.PoliticalClass;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.textFeatures.predict(
    "There are so many things you can learn from text."
);
Map&lt;PoliticalClass, Double&gt; result = single.getTextFeatures();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "There are so many things you can learn from text.",
    "You could use the features to train a model!"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.textFeatures.predict(example);
List&lt;Map&lt;PoliticalClass, Double&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getTextFeatures();
System.out.println(results);
</pre>

        <div id="intersections" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Intersections</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="intersections"></strong> <br>See correlations among the results of multiple APIs. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/apis/intersections/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-bind-html="apis"></span> - List - required - exactly two models you'd like to see correlations between<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> A nested dictionary with the first set of keys corresponding to the first API listed. These keys map to the values of the results from the second API listed. Finally, the keys on the second level map to the correlation between the two parent keys and the confidence is the model's confidence in this correlation. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# output (you must send multiple examples to use intersections)
{
    'twitter_engagement': {
        'sentiment_hq': {
            'confidence': 0.5330776330179838, 
            'correlation': 0.24545454545454548
        }
    }
}
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# output (you must send multiple examples to use intersections)
{
    'twitter_engagement': {
        'sentiment_hq': {
            'confidence': 0.5330776330179838, 
            'correlation': 0.24545454545454548
        }
    }
}
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">

        }
    }
}

          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

Map&lt;String, List&gt; params = new HashMap()
ArrayList&lt;String&gt; apiList = new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;;
apiList.add("twitter_engagement");
apiList.add("sentiment_hq");
params.put("apis", apiList);

// Using the first chapter of the Scarlet Letter as an example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.instersections.predict(
    prisonDoor,
    params
);
Map&lt;String, Map&lt;String, Map&lt;String, Double&gt;&gt;&gt; result = multiple.getIntersections();
System.out.println(result);
</pre>
