        <div id="analyze_text" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Analyze Text</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="analyze_text"></strong> <br>Make calls to many APIs in parallel. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/apis/multiapi/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - text to be analyzed<br> <span ng-bind-html="apis"></span> - List - required - the list of APIs to run in parallel<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> A dictionary where each key maps to the specified models' results. If used on a single input (not recommemnded as using multiple APIs quickly uses up your allotted calls!) you'll get the default response, otherwise a list of the default. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
{
    'sentiment_hq': 0.7300551533699036,
    'political': {
        'Conservative': 0.2288717527904388,
        'Green': 0.05575739681227337,
        'Liberal': 0.6541234047231098,
        'Libertarian': 0.06124744567417795
    }
}

          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

Map&lt;String, Object&gt; params = new HashMap&lt;&gt;()
ArrayList&lt;String&gt; apiList = new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;();
apiList.add("sentiment_hq");
apiList.add("political");
params.put("apis", apiList);

Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");

// single example
IndicoResult single  = indico.text.predict(
    "Democratic candidate Hillary Clinton is excited for the upcoming election.",
    params
);
Double result = single.getSentimentHQ();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "Democratic candidate Hillary Clinton is excited for the upcoming election.", 
    "Bill Clinton joins President Obama for a birthday golf game at Marthas Vineyard."
};

BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.text.predict(
    example,
    params
);
List&lt;Double&gt; result = multiple.getSentimentHQ();
System.out.println(result);
</pre>

        <div id="text_splitting" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Sentence Splitting</h2> 
          <p>If you'd like indico to automatically handle splitting your documents up into sentences or paragraphs to provide a more detailed analysis of your data, all of our text APIs feature a <code>split</code> keyword argument for providing sentence or paragraph level API results. </p> 
          <p>The valid options for the <code>split</code> keyword are <code>"sentence"</code> and <code>"paragraph"</code>. </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> A list of dictionaries, where each dictionary contains the <code>position</code>, <code>text</code>, and <code>results</code> keys. The <code>position</code> key contains information on the indexes into the original document, the <code>text</code> key contains the analyzed sentence or document, and the <code>results</code> key contains the output of the API. </p> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">[{u'position': [0, 23],
  u'results': 8.478955551191238e-05,
  u'text': u'This sentence is awful.'},
 {u'position': [24, 47],
  u'results': 0.9694245630414513,
  u'text': u'This sentence is great!'}]
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint">[{"position"=&gt;[0, 23], "results"=&gt;8.478955551191238e-05, "text"=&gt;"This sentence is awful."}, {"position"=&gt;[24, 47], "results"=&gt;0.9694245630414513, "text"=&gt;"This sentence is great!"}]
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint">

        <div id="image_analysis" class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Image Analysis</h2> 
          <p> Use our models to analyze text in a variety of contexts! </p> 
          <div class="function-list"> 
           <ul> 
            <li> <a href="#fer"><span ng-bind-html="fer"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#image_features"><span ng-bind-html="image_features"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#facial_features"><span ng-bind-html="facial_features"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#facial_localization"><span ng-bind-html="facial_localization"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#content_filtering"><span ng-bind-html="content_filtering"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#image_recognition"><span ng-bind-html="image_recognition"></span></a> </li> 
            <li> <a href="#analyze_image"><span ng-bind-html="analyze_image"></span></a> </li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> 
          <p class="thumbprint-args"> <br> <b ng-bind-html="data"></b> :<code>Filepath</code> or <code>Base64 Encoded Image</code>: required: The API processes strings as a single piece of text and return a single result. You can also send a list of phrases to be processed all in one call(more efficient).<br> <span ng-show="java"><b>[params]</b> :<code>Map</code>: optional: Some of the functions have optional parameters that are passed to the function with a map, the keys being the names of the options shown below.<br><br></span> <span ng-show="php"><b>[config]</b> :<code>Array</code>: optional: Some of the functions have optional parameters that are passed to the function with an array, the keys being the names of the options shown below.<br><br></span> <b ng-bind-html="api_key"></b> :<code>String</code>: required/optional: Your API key for authenticating your usage. If you haven't set your API key in <a href="#config">another way</a>, this is required.<br> <b ng-bind-html="cloud"></b> :<code>String</code>: optional: If specified, calls will be made to the private cloud address provided. If you haven't purchased private infrastructure from us then this input is irrelevant. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="image-format" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h2>Input Image Format</h2> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <div ng-show="python"> 
           <p>Images can be sent to the <code>indicoio</code> image analysis functions as URLs, file paths, base64 encoded images, numpy array objects, or <code>skimage</code> image objects. Sample code for loading in an image using skimage or <code>PIL</code> is provided below. Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Image URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">import indicoio

indicoio.fer('https://IMAGE_URL')</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Filepath</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">import indicoio

indicoio.fer('FILEPATH')</pre> 
           <p><strong>Formatting images using skimage</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">import skimage.io
import indicoio

pixel_array = skimage.io.imread('FILEPATH')

indicoio.fer(pixel_array)</pre> 
           <p><strong>Formatting images using PIL and numpy</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint python">from PIL import Image
import numpy as np
import indicoio

image = Image.load('FILEPATH')
pixel_array = np.array(image)

indicoio.fer(pixel_array)</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <div ng-show="ruby"> 
           <p>Images can be sent to the <code>indico</code> image analysis functions as URLs, file paths or base64 encoded JPEGs or PNGs. Sample code for loading in an image using the <code>base64</code> RubyGem is provided below. Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Image URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">require 'indico'

url = "https://IMAGE_URL"
Indico.fer(url)</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Filepath</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">require 'indico'

filepath = "PATH_TO_YOUR_IMAGE"
Indico.fer(filepath)</pre> 
           <p><strong>Formatting images using the Base64 RubyGem</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">require 'indico'
require 'base64'

filepath = "PATH_TO_YOUR_IMAGE"
base64data = Base64.encode64(File.open(filepath, "rb").read)
Indico.fer(base64data)</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <div ng-show="node"> 
           <p>Images must be sent to the <code>indico.io</code> image analysis functions as URLs or base64 encoded JPEGs or PNGs. Sample code for loading in an image using the <code>fs</code> Node package is provided below. Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Image URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">var indico = require('indico.io')
indico.apiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY";

indico.fer("https://IMAGE_URL")
  .then(function(res) {
    console.log(res);
  }).catch(function(err) {
    console.warn(err);
  });</pre> 
           <p><strong>Sending an image using fs</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">var indico = require('indico.io');
var fs = require('fs');

indico.apiKey = "YOUR_API_KEY";

var filename = "PATH_TO_YOUR_IMAGE";

fs.readFile(filename, function(err, data) {
  base64data = new Buffer(data).toString('base64');
  indico.fer(base64data)
  .then(function(res) {
    console.log(res);
  }).catch(function(err) {
    console.warn(err);
  });
});</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <div ng-show="java"> 
           <p>Images can be sent to the <code>indico</code> image analysis functions as Strings representing image URLs, file paths, BufferedImages and as File objects. Sample code for all three is provided below. Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <p><strong>Sending images through the API</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import javax.imageio.ImageIO;

Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
String filePath = "path/to/image.png";
String imageURL = "https://IMAGE_URL";

// From a URL
IndicoResult responseOne = indico.fer.predict(imageURL);

// As a String
IndicoResult responseTwo = indico.fer.predict(filePath);

// As a File
IndicoResult responseThree = indico.fer.predict(new File(filePath));

// As a BufferedImage
BufferedImage image = ImageIO.read(new File(filePath));
IndicoResult responseFour = indico.fer.predict(image, "png");</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <div ng-show="r"> 
           <p>Images can be sent to the <code>indicoio</code> image analysis functions as Strings representing image URLs or file paths.<br> Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <p><strong>Specifying Image URL</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">library(indicoio)

fer("https://IMAGE_URL")</pre> 
           <p><strong>Specifying filepath</strong></p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">library(indicoio)

fer("PATH_IMAGE_FILE")</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <div ng-show="php"> 
           <p>The <code>IndicoIo</code> image API requires image URLs, image filepaths or base64 encoded PNGs and JPGs. Instructions for loading images into this format are provided below.<br> Although images are scaled on our servers, use square crops for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected.</p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">&lt;?php

require(__DIR__ . '/vendor/autoload.php');
use \IndicoIo\IndicoIo as IndicoIo;

$url = "https://IMAGE_URL";
$filepath = "/path/to/image";

$im = file_get_contents($filepath);
$b64data = base64_encode($im);

IndicoIo::fer($url);
IndicoIo::fer($filepath);
IndicoIo::fer($b64data);
?&gt;</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- JS with jQuery --> 
          <div ng-show="js"> 
           <p> In your javascript examples we'll be using jQuery ($) to make requests to indico.<br> Sending JPG and PNG images to our API is also possible with plain Javascript! You can either provide a url that links to the image or a base64 encoded image.<br> Although images are scaled on our servers, try to use square crops when possible for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected. </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">$.post('https://apiv2.indico.io/fer,
  JSON.stringify({
    api_key: "YOUR_API_KEY",
    data: "image-url or base64_image"
  })
).then(function(res) { console.log(res) });</pre> 
          </div> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <div ng-show="curl"> 
           <p> Sending JPG and PNG images to our API is also possible with cURL! It requires that you base64 encode the image and send the new representation to our API.<br> Although images are scaled on our servers, try to use square crops when possible for optimal performance. Both single and batch image requests of over 15 MB will be rejected. </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/fer' -d '{"data": "https://IMAGE_URL"}'

b64=$(cat example.png | base64)
echo "{\"data\":\"$b64\"}" &gt; data.json
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/fer' -d @data.json</pre> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"></div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="fer" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Facial Emotion Recognition</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="fer" class="prettyprint"></strong><br> Determine the emotions expressed in an image of a human face. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/fer/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="detect"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - When True, FER detects all faces in the image and returns their locations with a FER dictionary for each face (see Output for more information)<br> <span ng-bind-html="sensitivity"></span> - Float (defaults to .8) - optional - The certainty threshold (between 0 and 1) the model uses to decide what to return as a face. Only used when <code>detect</code> is True.<br><br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with 6 key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that each of 6 detectable emotions are expressed by the face in the analyzed image. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the emotions (Angry, Sad, Neutral, Surprise, Fear, Happy) and the values are the probabilities that the face in the analyzed image is expressing each emotion.<br> <br> Values less than 0.05 indicate that it is very unlikely the face is expressing the corresponding emotion.<br> <br> Using the detect flag changes output format: When using the detect flag the results returned will be a list of dictionaries. Each dictionary in the list corresponds to a detected face. Each dictionary has two key-value pairs, the keys are "emotions" and "location". The value of "emotions" is the same dictionary described above with 6 key-value pairs. The value of "location" is the bounding box of the detected face in the form [x position of top left corner, y position of top-left corner, width of bounding box, height of bounding box].<br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message -->

var indico = require('indico.io');
indico.apiKey =  'YOUR_API_KEY';

var response = function(res) { console.log(res); }
var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }
  
// single example
indico.fer("&lt;IMAGE&gt;")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;",
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
];
indico.fer(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.image.FacialEmotion;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.fer.predict(
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
);
Map&lt;FacialEmotion, Double&gt; result = single.getFer();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;", 
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.fer.predict(example);
List&lt;Map&lt;FacialEmotion, Double&gt;&gt; results = multiple.getFer();
System.out.println(results);
</pre>

        <div id="image_features" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Image Features</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="image_features" class="prettyprint"></strong><br> Convert images into meaningful feature vectors.<br> Extracts abstract image features for use as inputs to learning algorithms. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/imagefeatures/[batch]/?version=[version]</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> <span ng-bind-html="version"></span> - Integer (defaults to 3) - optional - the version of the model to use (2, or 3; see output for more information)<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> List of 4096 numbers (floats). Each number corresponds to the strength of that feature in the feature vector. Version 3 is the highest quality and has the lowest error rate. Version 1 has been deprecated. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message -->

import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.imageFeatures.predict(
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
);
Double result = single.getImageFeatures();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;", 
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.imageFeatures.predict(example);
List&lt;Double&gt; results = multiple.getImageFeatures();
System.out.println(results);

        <div id="facial_features" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Facial Features</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="facial_features" class="prettyprint"></strong><br> Convert images of human faces into meaningful feature vectors.<br> Extracts abstract image features for use as inputs to learning algorithms. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/facialfeatures/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="detect"></span> - Boolean (defaults to True) - optional - When True, fer detects all faces in the image and returns the location and fer dictionary for each face (see Output for more information)<br> <span ng-bind-html="sensitivity"></span> - Float (defaults to .8) - optional - The certainty threshold (between 0 and 1) the model uses to decide what to return as a face. Only used when 'detect is True.<br> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> List of 48 numbers (floats). Each number corresponds to the strength of that feature in the feature vector. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message -->

        <div id="facial_localization" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Facial Localization</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="facial_localization"></strong><br> Returns a list of face bounding boxes found in a given image.<br> Available for version 0.8 and later. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/faciallocalization/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="sensitivity"></span> - Float (defaults to .8) - optional - The certainty threshold (between 0 and 1) the model uses to decide what to return as a face<br> <span ng-bind-html="crop"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - If set to True, output is a list of cropped face images, each represented by a two dimensional array of integer pixel values<br> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a list of dictionaries that map from "top_left_corner" and "bottom_right_corner" to pixel coordinate pairs. Each mapping uniquely identifies a facial bounding box. The origin (0, 0) is assumed to be upper left corner. If the `crop` flag is set to True, output will instead be a list of the two dimensional pixel arrays of those images. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
{
    'top_left_corner': (10, 24),
    'bottom_right_corner': : (87, 96),
}

# batch output
[
    {
        'top_left_corner': (10, 24),
        'bottom_right_corner': : (87, 96),
    }, 
    {
        'top_left_corner': (10, 24),
        'bottom_right_corner': : (87, 96),
    }
]
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">

        <div id="content_filtering" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Content Filtering</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="content_filtering"></strong><br> Determines whether or not an image contains mature content.<br> Available for version 0.8 and later. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/contentfiltering/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a number between 0 and 1. This number is a probability representing the likelihood that the analyzed image has offensive content. Values greater than 0.5 indicate that the image most likely contains offensive content, while values less than 0.5 indicate that the image probably does not contain offensive content. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# single output
0.9782025594088044

# batch output
[
    0.9782025594088044, 
    0.3782025594088044
]

        <div id="image_recognition" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Image Recognition</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="image_recognition"></strong> <br>Determines the subject of an image. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/imagerecognition/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - refer to <a href="#image-format">img format guide</a> - required<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="top_n"></span> - Integer - optional - only return this many of the most likely category<br> <span ng-bind-html="threshold"></span> - Float (defaults to 0.) - optional - only return category with likelihood greater than this number<br> <span ng-bind-html="hq"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, uses a higher quality model that is slower for batch requests <br><br> <span ng-show="js || curl"> For an example of how to pass keyword arguments to the indico API in a post request, see the right hand sidebar. </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> This function will return a dictionary with 1000 key-value pairs. These key-value pairs represent the likelihood that the analyzed image is one of 1000 possible subjects. The keys in the dictionary are strings containing the subject names and the values are the probabilities that the analyzed image is of each subject.<br> </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON -->

var logError = function(err) { console.log(err); }

// single example
indico.imageRecognition("&lt;IMAGE&gt;")
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

// batch example
var batchInput = [
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;",
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
];
indico.imageRecognition(batchInput)
  .then(response)
  .catch(logError);

          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.IndicoResult;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.imageRecognition.predict(
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
);
Double result = single.getImageRecognition();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] example = {
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;",
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;"
};
BatchIndicoResult multiple = indico.imageRecognition.predict(example);
List&lt;Double&gt; results = multiple.getImageRecognition();
System.out.println(results);
</pre>

        <div id="analyze_image" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Analyze Image</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="analyze_image"></strong> <br>Make calls to many APIs in parallel. </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/apis/multiapi/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - image or list of images - required - images to be analyzed<br> <span ng-bind-html="apis"></span> - list - required - the list of APIs to run in parallel<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> A dictionary where each key maps to the specified models' results. If used on a single input (not recommemnded as using multiple APIs quickly uses up your allotted calls!) you'll get the default response, otherwise a list of the default. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- should be macro'ed to accept 6 keys, 6 values, and an omitted message --> 
          <!-- PYTHON -->

          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
import io.indico.Indico;
import io.indico.api.image.FacialEmotion;
import io.indico.api.BatchIndicoResult;

Map&lt;String, List&gt; params = new HashMap()
ArrayList&lt;String&gt; apiList = new ArrayList&lt;String&gt;;
apiList.add("image_features");
apiList.add("fer");
params.put("apis", apiList);

// single example
Indico indico = new Indico("YOUR_API_KEY");
IndicoResult single = indico.analyzeImage.predict(
    "&lt;IMAGE&gt;",
    params
);
Map&lt;String, Map&lt;FacialEmotion, Double&gt;&gt; result = single.getAnalyzeImage();
System.out.println(result);

// batch example
String[] batchExample = {
    &lt;IMAGE&gt;, 
    &lt;IMAGE&gt;
};
BatchIndicoResult batch = indico.analyzeImage.predict(batchExample,
    params
);
Map&lt;String, ArrayList&lt;Map&lt;FacialEmotion, Double&gt;&gt;&gt; result = batch.getAnalyzeImage();
System.out.println(result);
</pre>

       <div class="method" id="custom"> 
        <div id="about_custom" class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>About Custom Collection</h3> 
          <p> Not everyone's needs align with what indico offers out of the box, so we also provide a generalized solution that learns to recognize patterns in <b>your</b> data. This means that you can apply our technology to a specific use case, as well as train your model on the data most relevant to you.<br> <br> <strong>What is this?</strong><br> It's a way to automatically learn about new data based on the patterns in past data. For example, if you had a photo sharing app with user specified scene tags, you could use 4,000 tagged photos to predict tags for the remaining 17,000 untagged ones. Right now we support one label per input, but there are <a href="https://indico.io/blog/fashion-matching-tutorial/">ways to work around that</a>.<br> <br> <strong>Who is this for?</strong><br> Anyone who currently has to label text or image data by hand or has ever shied away from building great things that might require continuous, manual labelling.<br> <br> <strong>What do I need?</strong><br> All you need is a <b>well defined problem</b>. Say you want to see what kinds of posts your followers like. If you took the text from your posts and passed the amount of likes for each one as a label, you could create a Collection that predicts how much your audience will like new posts. If you're working with a completely unlabeled dataset, you and your team can use our <a href="https://indico.io/product/crowdlabel">CrowdLabel</a> tool to seamlessly and quickly upload, label, and process data. You can then train a Custom Collection on your newly labeled dataset.<br> <br> <strong>How much do I need?</strong><br> This one's a bit of a gray area depending on your application. Having very little data is rarely helpful, but having huge amounts doesn't guarantee accurate predictions either. For starters, you should aim for your data to only communicate relevant information. Having a border on all your nature photos could cause your image classifier to believe any bordered image represents nature. To give you a better idea, here's a table that describes how many samples per label you ought to start with on tasks of varying difficulties:<br> </p> 
          <table class="benchmark table"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th>Task</th> 
             <th>Text Samples </th> 
             <th>Image Samples </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>Easy</td> 
             <td>100</td> 
             <td>10</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>Medium</td> 
             <td>500</td> 
             <td>50</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>Hard</td> 
             <td>2000</td> 
             <td>200</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <br> 
          <p> <strong>How many samples can I add?</strong><br> Custom Collections is designed to provide high quality predictions with as few data points as possible. In general, you'll see diminishing returns after the first few thousand data points. Because of this, the Custom Collections API currently has a cap at <b>50,000 samples</b>. If you want to train Collections with larger amounts of input data, reach out to us directly at contact@indico.io and we'll help make your project possible. </p> 
          <p> <strong>What makes a task hard for a computer?</strong><br> As humans, we know that subtle variations can make a world of difference. We're always working on teaching machine learning models to retain as much useful context as possible, but catching slight cues can be difficult to do in a generalized way. Here are some example categorization tasks for text and image Collections.<br> </p> 
          <table class="benchmark table"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th>Task</th> 
             <th>Text</th> 
             <th>Image</th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody>
            <tr> 
             <td>Easy</td> 
             <td>Wallstreet Journal vs. Buzzfeed</td> 
             <td>Jungle vs. Beach</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>Medium</td> 
             <td>1 Star vs. 5 Star Review</td> 
             <td>Leather vs. Wood</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td>Hard</td> 
             <td>Dieting vs. Fitness</td> 
             <td>Husky vs. Malamute</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <p> </p>
         </div> 
        </div>

         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Benchmarking Custom Collection</h3> 
          <strong>How will my model's accuracy compare to other common techniques?</strong>
          <br> Especially with small amounts of data, Custom Collections should generally give a higher accuracy than common DIY algorithms. We benchmarked Custom Collections againts some common algorithms for three typical machine learning tasks to give an idea of how it compares.
          <br> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> <br> <strong>Task:</strong> Sentiment Detection (Text) <br> <strong>Dataset: <a href="http://ai.stanford.edu/~amaas/data/sentiment/"> Large Movie Review Dataset</a></strong> <br> <strong>Custom Collection Domain:</strong> "sentiment" <br> <strong>Benchmarked Against:</strong> tfidf vectors of samples (with stop words removed) into logistic regression with a grid search for an optimal regularization parameter <br> </p> 
          <table class="benchmark table"> 
           <tbody>

             <th>DIY Algorithm Accuracy</th> 
            </tr>

             <td>0.89</td> 
             <td>0.58</td> 
            </tr>

             <td>0.93</td> 
             <td>0.82</td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr>

             <td>0.86</td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> 
          <p> <br> <strong>Task:</strong> Topic Classification (Text, 4 Categories) <br> <strong>Dataset: <a href="https://www.di.unipi.it/~gulli/AG_corpus_of_news_articles.html"> Aggregated News</a></strong> <br> <strong>Custom Collection Domain:</strong> "topics" <br> <strong>Benchmarked Against:</strong> tfidf vectors of samples (with stop words removed) into logistic regression with a grid search for an optimal regularization parameter <br> </p>

          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// In the following examples we'll be using jQuery ($) to make requests to indico
function sendToIndico(endpoint, data, callback) {
  var key = 'YOUR_API_KEY',
    collectionName = 'my_collection',
    url = 'https://apiv2.indico.io'+ endpoint,
    log = function(res) { console.log(res) };

  var callback = callback || log;

  $.post(url, JSON.stringify({
    api_key: key,
    data: data,
    collection: 'my_collection'
  }), callback);
}

// Add data to your Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/batch/add_data', [
  ['text_sample1', 'label1'],
  ['text_sample2', 'label2'],
  ...
]);

// Train your Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/train', {});

// wait until the Collection is ready to predict
var waitForCollection = setInterval(function() {
  sendToIndico('/custom/collections', {},
    function(res) {
      res = JSON.parse(res);
      res = res['results']['my_collection'];
      if (res['status'] === 'ready') {
        // you're ready to make predictions!
        sendToIndico('/custom/predict', 'yay!');
        clearInterval(waitForCollection);
      } else {
        console.log('not yet...', res);
      }
    }
  );
}, 1000);

// If you've already trained the Collection as shown above, predicting is simpler
sendToIndico('/custom/batch/predict', ['so', 'easy!']);
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Create a collection by providing data
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/batch/add_data' --data '{"data": [["text1", "label1"], ["text2", "label2"], ...], "collection": "my_collection" }'

# Train your Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/train' --data '{"collection": "my_collection" }'

# Check the status of your Collections
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/collections' --data '{}'

# When it's ready, make predictions!
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/batch/predict' --data '{"data": ["now", "it\u0027s","done!"], "collection": "my_collection" }'
</pre>

        <div id="create" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>Creating a Collection</h3> 
          <p> Building your own Collection is simple! All you need is some labelled text or image data. Before we handle data, we first need to create our Collection object.<br> <br> If the Collection name that you specified has already been created, the command to the right will create a new object that represents the existing Collection. If not, a new one will be created.<br> <br> <b>Note:</b> There's no need to create a Collection when making calls directly to our URL endpoints. In that case, simply <code>POST</code> the name of the Collection along with the appropriate data outlined in the following sections. <br> <br> <b>The <code>domain</code> argument</b><br> If you're trying to build a Collection similar to one of indico's existing text APIs, you may be able to improve your Collection's performance by adapting one of our models to your domain's use case. If you set a domain when creating a Collection, you don't need to set it when adding data; the Collection will remember what its domain is! Currently, the following settings are valid for the <code>domain</code> argument: </p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><b><code>"standard"</code></b> - general text analysis problems</li> 
           <li><b><code>"topics"</code></b> - text classification problems similar to Text Tags</li> 
           <li><b><code>"sentiment"</code></b> - sentiment analysis and related problems</li> 
           <li><b><code>"finance"</code></b> - financial news and reports</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p> <b>The <code>shared</code> argument</b><br> You can set <code>shared</code> to <code>true</code> to access a Collection that someone else has given you access to via the <a href="#sharing">sharing methods</a> or a publicly <a href="publishing">published</a> Collection. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- ALWAYS SHOW --> 
          <pre class="prettyprint" ng-show="python || ruby || curl">
# For the sake of saving space we assume that
# the steps outlined below are done sequentially

</pre> 
          <pre class="prettyprint" ng-hide="python || ruby || curl">

// the steps outlined below are done sequentially

</pre> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">

collection = Collection("my_collection", domain='sentiment')

# Accessing a shared Collection
collection = Collection("shared_collection", domain="sentiment", shared=True)
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY -->

// function in the docs below

function sendToIndico(endpoint, data, callback) {
  var key = 'YOUR_API_KEY',
    collectionName = 'my_collection',
    url = 'https://apiv2.indico.io'+ endpoint,
    log = function(res) { console.log(res) };

  var callback = callback || log;

  // Using jQuery ($) to make requests
  $.post(url, JSON.stringify({
    api_key: key,
    data: data,
    collection: collectionName
  }), callback);
}

        <div id="add" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Adding data to your Collection</h3> 
          <p> Let's say we have a list of 4,000 images labeled with the scene they were taken in. If you're working in JavaScript or you don't have URLs or filenames for your images, you need to Base64 encode them first, which can be done <a href="#image-format">in your programming language of choice</a> or <a href="https://b64.io/">online</a>.<br> <br> Now we can send the data along with our labels as shown at right. Your Collection is going to attempt to learn patterns that associate the labels you provide with the data they correspond to.<br> <br> <b>The <code>domain</code> argument</b><br> If you're trying to build a Collection similar to one of indico's existing text APIs, you may be able to improve your Collection's performance by adapting one of our models to your domain's use case. Currently, the following settings are valid for the <code>domain</code> argument: </p> 
          <ul> 
           <li><b><code>"standard"</code></b> - general text analysis problems</li> 
           <li><b><code>"topics"</code></b> - text classification problems similar to Text Tags</li> 
           <li><b><code>"sentiment"</code></b> - sentiment analysis and related problems</li> 
           <li><b><code>"finance"</code></b> - financial news and reports</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p> Adding data does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint up python">
# String data
collection.add_data(["string", "label"])

# Image data
collection.add_data(["image-url or b64-image", "label"])

# Batch add data
collection.add_data([["string1", "label1"], ["string2", "label2"]])

# Specifying domain
collection.add_data([["string1", "label1"], ["string2", "label2"]], domain="topics")
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY -->

        <div id="remove" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Removing data from your Collection</h3> 
          <p> A situation may arise where you'd like certain data that you've added to not be considered by your Collection. This is simple to fix! It's very similar to adding data, but without the labels. </p> 
          <p> Removing data does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# String data
collection.remove_example("string")

# Image data
collection.remove_example("image-url or b64-image")

# Batch remove data
collection.remove_example(["string1", "string2", ...])
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# String data
collection.remove_example("string")

# Image data
collection.remove_example("image-url or b64-image")

# Batch remove data
collection.remove_example(["string1", "string2", ...])
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">  
// String data
collection.removeExample("string")
  .then(console.log);

// Image data
collection.removeExample("image-url or b64-image")
  .then(console.log);

// Batch remove data
collection.removeExample(["string1", "string2", ...])
  .then(console.log);

          <!-- JAVA -->

    "string", "string"
  ));

         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="train" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Training your new Collection</h3> 
          <p> Once you've added the desired data to your Collection, all you need to do is train and you'll be ready to analyze!<br> <br> You'll see in the code to the right of your screen how simple it is to train a Collection. However, you should keep in mind whether you'd like your code to wait until the model is trained or not. The following block is the status returned by <code>.train()</code>. </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
{
    'model_type': 'classification',
    'input_type': 'image',
    'number_of_examples': 4000,
    'permissions': {'read': [], 'write': []},
    'public': False,
    'registered': False,
    'status': 'training'
}
</pre> 
          <p> Adding <code>.wait()</code> will block until the training is complete. Otherwise you'll need to check the status (which we'll show you how to do below) of your new Collection separately and make sure it's ready before using it in analysis.<br> </p> 
          <p> Since Collection training is resource intensive, each call to `train` is counted as 100 API calls regardless of your Collection size. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# Training
collection.train()

# Telling Collection to block until ready
collection.wait()
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# Training
collection.train()

# Telling Collection to block until ready
collection.wait()
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// Training
collection.train()
  .then(console.log);

// Waiting for Collection to be ready
collection.train()
  .wait().then(function() {
    // collection ready to predict!
  });
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
  // Train
  newCollection.train();

  // Tell Collection to block until ready
  newCollection.waitUntilReady();
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
#Training
train(collection)

#Tell collection to block until ready
wait(collection)
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">
&lt;?php

//Training
$collection-&gt;train();

// Telling Collection to block until ready
$collection-&gt;wait();

?&gt;
</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// Train Collection
sendToIndico('custom/train', {});

// Without a client library you'll have to manually check the status of your collection as shown below
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Train Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/train' --data '{"collection": "my_collection" }'

# Without a client library you'll have to manually check the status of your collection as shown below
</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="status" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Checking the status of your Collections</h3> 
          <p> Whether you have mutliple Collections or would like to train a particularly large one and can't wait for it to finish, checking status is key to managing your Collection.<br> <br> Among other information, checking your Collection's status returns metrics which help evaluate how useful your Collection is at solving the intended task. For classification problems, this means a mean class accuracy score and per-class <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precision_and_recall">precision and recall scores.</a> For regression problems, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_absolute_error">mean absolute error</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_squared_error">mean squared error</a> metrics are returned. By inspecting these scores you can evaluate whether or not adding additonal data to your Collection or changing the Collection domain mayb be useful for improving the quality of your predictions. Please note that classification Collections may not return metrics if some of the classes have less than 10 examples. Here's a sample response from calling <code>collections():</code> </p>
          <pre class="prettyprint">
{
    'image_tagger': {
        'model_type': 'classification',
        'input_type': 'image',
        'number_of_examples': 4000,
        'status': 'ready',
        'permissions': {
        	'read': [],
        	'write': []
        },
        'metrics': {
        	'class_accuracy': 0.875,
        	'precision': {
        		'cat': 0.9,
        		'dog': 0.875
        	},
        	'recall': {
        		'cat': 0.85,
        		'dog': 1.0
        	}
        },
        'public': False,
        'registered': False,
    },
    'detect_rapper': {
        'model_type': 'classification',
        'input_type': 'text',
        'number_of_examples': 120000,
        'status': 'ready',
        'permissions': {
        	'read': [],
        	'write': []
        },
        'public': False,
        'registered': False,
        ...
    }, ...
}
</pre> 
          <p> Checking the status of your Collection does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# Check status of current Collection
collection.info()

# Checking all of your Collections requires a separate function
from indicoio.custom import collections

collections()
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# Checking status of your current Collection
collection.info()

# Check all of your Collections
Indico::collections()
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// Check status of current collection
collection.info()
  .then(console.log);

// Check status of all your collections
indico.collections()
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
// Check status of current collection
Map&lt;String, ?&gt; collectionInfo = indico.custom.info(collectionName)

// Check status of all your collections
Map&lt;String, Map&lt;String, ?&gt;&gt; collectionsInfo = indico.custom.getAllCollections();
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
# Check status of current collection
info(collection)

# Check status of all your collections
collections()
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">
&lt;?php

// Check status of current Collection
$collection-&gt;info()

// Check status of all your collections
IndicoIo::collections()

?&gt;
</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// Get status of all your Collections
sendToIndico('/custom/collections', {});
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Get status of all your Collections
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/collections' --data '{}'
</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="predict" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Analyzing new data!</h3> 
          <p> Now your model is ready to predict labels for new data samples. All you need to do is pass a <code>String</code> if you created a text Collection or a Base64 encoded image if you created an image Collection.<br> <br> The response will be a mapping of the classes you've provided to their predicted likelihood. For our photo example, each class is a scene tag, like "nature", "city", or "space". </p> 
          <pre class="prettyprint">
{"nature": 0.938..., "city": 0.122..., "space": 0.055...}</pre> 
          <p> If you've set your data <code>domain</code> to something other than <code>"standard"</code>, make sure to pass in the same value when predicting on new examples. </p> 
          <p> If you've trained a Collection for a classification task (predicting which categories text or an image belongs to), the following keyword arguments are supported. </p> 
          <p> <code>[top_n]</code> - Integer - optionals - only return this many of the most likely topics. </p> 
          <p> <code>[threshold]</code> - Float (defaults to 0.) - optional - only return topics with likelihood greater than this number. </p> 
          <p> <code>[independent]</code> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when False, the probabilities of all topics sum to 1, when True, topic probabilities are independent and are not constrained to sum to 1. You must have more than two output categories in order to make use of this flag. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# String data
collection.predict("string")

# Image data
collection.predict("image-url or b64-image")

# Making batch predictions
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...])

# Specifying domain
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...], domain="topics")
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# String data
collection.predict("string")

# Image data
collection.predict("image-url or b64-image")

# Making batch predictions
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...])

# Specifying domain
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...], {domain: "topics"})
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// String data
collection.predict("string")
  .then(console.log);

// Image data
collection.predict("image-url or b64-image")
  .then(console.log);

// Making batch predictions
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...])
  .then(console.log);

// Specifying domain
collection.predict(["string1", "string2", ...], {domain: "topics"})
  .then(console.log);
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
// String data
newCollection.predict();

// Image data
newCollection.predict();

// Making batch predictions
newCollection.predict(Arrays.asList(
    "string",
    "string"
    // ...
));

Map&lt;String, Object&gt; params = new HashMap&lt;String, String&gt;() {­{
    put("domain", "topics");
}­};

// Specifying domain
newCollection.predict(Arrays.asList(
    "string",
    "string"
    // ...
), params);
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
# String data
predict(collection, "string")

# Image data
predict(collection, "image-url or b64-image")

# Making batch predictions
batch &lt;- list(list(, ), list(, ))
predict(collection, batch)

# Specifying domain
predict(collection, batch, domain = "topics")
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">
&lt;?php 

// String data
$result = $collection-&gt;predict("string");

// Image data
$result = $collection-&gt;predict("image-url or b64-image");

// Making batch predictions

    list("string", "string")
);

// Specifying domain
$result = $collection-&gt;predict([
    ,
    
]), array("domain" =&gt; "topics"));

?&gt;
</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// String data
sendToIndico('custom/predict', "string");

// Image data
sendToIndico('custom/predict', "image-url or b64-image");

// Making batch predictions
sendToIndico('custom/batch/predict', ["string1", "string2", ...])

// Specifying domain
sendToIndico('custom/batch/predict?domain=topics', ["string1", "string2", ...])
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">

# Image data
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/predict' --data '{"data": "image-url or b64-image", "collection": "my_collection" }'

# Making batch predictions
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/batch/predict' --data '{"data": ["string1", "string2", ...], "collection": "my_collection" }'

# Specifying domain
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/batch/predict?domain=topics' --data '{"data": ["string1", "string2", ...], "collection": "my_collection" }'
</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="rename" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Renaming a Collection</h3> 
          <p> We provide a way to rename your Collection. Just call <code>.rename(new_name)</code> on the Collection instance with a new Collection name. </p> 
          <p> Renaming your Collection does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# Rename your current Collection
collection.rename("new_collection_name")
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# Rename your current Collection
collection.rename("new_collection_name")
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// Rename your current collection
collection.rename("new_collection_name")
  .then(console.log);
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
// Rename your current collection
collection.rename("new_collection_name");
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
# Rename your current collection
collection &lt;- rename(collection, "new_collection_name")
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">

// Rename your current Collection
$collection-&gt;rename("new_collection_name");

          <!-- JS -->

          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">

</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="sharing" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Sharing a Collection</h3> 
          <p> You can share your Collection to enable specific users to read and/or write to the Collection. </p> 
          <p> To do so, you must first register the Collection by calling <code>.register(public)</code> on Collection, setting <code>make_public</code> to <code>true</code> or <code>false</code>. Then, you can authorize certain emails to read or write by calling <code>.authorize(email, permission)</code> with <code>"read"</code> or <code>"write"</code> as the permission. </p> 
          <p> Other users must pass in <code>shared</code> to the Collection object as a Boolean to indicate whether or not the Collection is shared with them. A shared Collection must have a name unique across all shared Collections. </p> 
          <p> You can deregister the Collection by calling <code>.deregister()</code> on the Collection and deauthorize users by calling <code>.deauthorize(email)</code> on theCollection. </p> 
          <p> Registering Collections and authorizing users do not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
collection.register(make_public=False)
collection.authorize("contact@indico.io", "write")

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
collection.deauthorize("contact@indico.io")

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
collection.register(make_public=False)
collection.authorize("contact@indico.io", "write")

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
collection.deauthorize("contact@indico.io")

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
collection.register(make_public=False)
          .authorize("contact@indico.io", "write")

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
collection.deauthorize("contact@indico.io")

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
collection.register(false);
collection.authorize("contact@indico.io", PERMISSION.WRITE);

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
collection.deauthorize("contact@indico.io");

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister();
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
register(collection)
authorize(collection, "contact@indico.io", "write")

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
deauthorize(collection, "contact@indico.io")

# Deregister Collection
deregister(collection)
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">
&lt;?php

// Register Collection as a sharable collection
$collection-&gt;register();
$collection-&gt;authorize("contact@indico.io", "write");

// Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
$collection-&gt;deauthorize("contact@indico.io");

// Deregister Collection
$collection-&gt;deregister();

?&gt;
</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// Register Collection as a sharable collection
sendToIndico('/custom/register', {"make_public": false});
sendToIndico('/custom/authorize', {"email": "contact@indico.io", "permission_type": "write"});

// Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/deauthorize', {"email": "contact@indico.io"});

// Deregister Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/deregister', {});
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Register Collection as a sharable collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/register' --data '{"collection": "collection", "make_public": false}'
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/authorize' --data '{"collection": "collection", "email": "contact@indico.io", "permission_type": "write"}'

# Deauthorize contact@indico.io from Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/deauthorize' --data '{"collection": "collection", "email": "contact@indico.io"}'
# Deregister Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/deregister' --data '{"collection": "collection"}'

</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="publishing" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Publishing a Collection</h3> 
          <p> You can share your Collection with the public for read only access. A shared Collection must have a name unique across all shared Collections. </p> 
          <p> To do so, you can register the Collection by calling <code>.register(public)</code> on Collection with <code>true</code> for public. Other users must pass in <code>shared</code> to the Collection object as a Boolean to indicate whether or not the Collection is shared with them. </p> 
          <p> You can un-publish the Collection by calling <code>.deregister()</code> on the Collection. </p> 
          <p> Registering Collections does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
collection.register(make_public=True)

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- RUBY --> 
          <pre ng-show="ruby" class="prettyprint ruby">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
collection.register(make_public=True)

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
collection.register(make_public=true)

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister()
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
collection.register(true);

# Deregister Collection
collection.deregister();
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
register(collection, TRUE)

# Deregister Collection
deregister(collection)
</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">
&lt;?php

// Register Collection as a published collection.
$collection-&gt;register(True);

// Deregister Collection
$collection-&gt;deregister();

?&gt;
</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// Register Collection as a published collection.
sendToIndico('/custom/register', {"make_public": true});

// Deregister Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/deregister', {});
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Register Collection as a published collection.
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/register' --data '{"collection": "collection", "make_public": true}'

# Deregister Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/deregister' --data '{"collection": "collection"}'

</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div id="delete" class="method-section clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <h3>Deleting a Collection</h3> 
          <p> Eventually you may find that you no longer need a Collection, so we provide a way to delete it. Just call <code>.clear()</code> on the Collection instance. </p> 
          <p> Clearing your Collection does not count towards your monthly call volume. </p> 
         </div> 
         <div class="method-example"> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON -->

</pre> 
          <!-- NODE --> 
          <pre ng-show="node" class="prettyprint node">
// Delete current Collection
collection.clear()
  .then(console.log);
</pre> 
          <!-- JAVA --> 
          <pre ng-show="java" class="prettyprint java">
// Delete current Collection
collection.clear();
</pre> 
          <!-- R --> 
          <pre ng-show="r" class="prettyprint r">

</pre> 
          <!-- PHP --> 
          <pre ng-show="php" class="prettyprint php">

</pre> 
          <!-- JS --> 
          <pre ng-show="js" class="prettyprint js">
// Delete current Collection
sendToIndico('/custom/clear_collection', {});
</pre> 
          <!-- cURL --> 
          <pre ng-show="curl" class="prettyprint curl">
# Delete current Collection
curl -H 'X-ApiKey: YOUR_API_KEY' 'https://apiv2.indico.io/custom/clear_collection' --data '{"collection": my_collection }'
</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
       </div> 
       <!--########################### PDF EXTRACTION ###########################--> 
       <div class="method" id="pdf_extraction"> 
        <div class="method-section start clearfix"> 
         <div class="method-description"> 
          <hr> 
          <h3>PDF Extraction</h3> 
          <p> <strong ng-bind-html="pdf_extraction" class="prettyprint"></strong><br> Extract images, body text, metadata, and tables from PDF documents.<br> </p> 
          <div ng-show="js || curl"> 
           <span class="info">Private cloud endpoint</span> 
           <p> <strong><code>POST</code> https://[cloud].indico.domains/facialfeatures/[batch]/</strong> </p> 
          </div> 
          <span class="info">Arguments</span> 
          <p> <span ng-bind-html="data"></span> - String | List - required - filename of PDF to be analyzed<br> <span ng-hide="js || curl"> <span ng-bind-html="api_key"></span> - String - optional - your indico API key<br> <span ng-bind-html="cloud"></span> - String - optional - your private cloud subdomain<br> </span> <span ng-bind-html="images"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, returns all the images in the PDF file in <a href="http://pillow.readthedocs.io/en/3.4.x/handbook/concepts.html">PIL format</a><br> <span ng-bind-html="text"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, returns all body text (separately from headers, footers, and tables)<br> <span ng-bind-html="metadata"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, returns the following: tagged, form, producer, author, encryption status, program used to create the file, file size, PDF version, optimised, modification date, title, creation date, number of pages, page size<br> <span ng-bind-html="tables"></span> - Boolean (defaults to False) - optional - when True, returns the contents of tables in the document, separately from body text<br> </p> 
          <span class="info">Output</span> 
          <p> PDF Extraction returns the extracted information in JSON format so you can easily transfer the data to Custom Collections for training your own machine learning models, or for analysis using our pre-trained models. If you need someone to label the data, you can reformat the data and save as a CSV for use with CrowdLabel. </p> 
          <!-- Input String --> 
          <!-- PYTHON --> 
          <pre ng-show="python" class="prettyprint python">

import indicoio
indicoio.config.api_key = 'YOUR_API_KEY'

# single example
indicoio.pdf_extraction("filename")

# batch example
indicoio.pdf_extraction([
    "filename",
    "filename2"

   <script type="text/javascript">
        var user_data = {
            user_id: '',
            cookie_id: "1c480a98691bdcb7ec3a2111e49c8861",
            ip: '',
            origin: window.location.pathname
        };
        
        $(function() {
            var getProps = function(self) {
                return $.extend({
                    dest: $(self).attr('href'),
                    name: $(self).text(),
                }, user_data);
            };

            analytics.page($(this).attr('href'), user_data);
            analytics.track('Viewed Page', $.extend({
                name: window.location.pathname,
                search: window.location.search
            }, user_data));

            $('.navbar-left li').click(function() {
                analytics.track('Navbar Clicked', getProps(this)); 
            });

            $('.cta').click(function() {
                analytics.track('Clicked CTA', getProps(this));
            });   

            $('.split-test clickable').click(function() {
                var test = $(this).closest('.split-test');
                var testName = test.attr('name');
                var seen = test.attr('split');

                analytics.track('AB Test - Clicked '+testName, {
                    'clicked': seen
                });
            });

            $('.open-intercom').click(function() { $('#intercom-launcher').click(); })
        });
        function clientsideFormHandler(form_id, post_url){
            Messenger.options = {
                extraClasses: 'messenger-fixed messenger-on-top',
                theme: 'block'
            }

            $(form_id).submit( function(e) {
                e.preventDefault();

                var valid = true;
                $(form_id+' [req="true"]').each(function(index, input) {
                    if ($(input).val() == '') {
                        valid = false;
                        return false
                    }
                })
                if (valid == false) {
                    Messenger().post({
                        message: "Please fill in all required fields",
                        type: 'error',
                        hideAfter: 3
                    });
                    $('html, body').animate({ 
                        scrollTop: ($(form_id).offset().top - 120).toString() + 'px'
                    });
                    return false;
                }

                var form = e.currentTarget
                var form_data = {};
                $.each(e.currentTarget, function(i) {
                    if (form[i].type != 'submit'){
                        form_data[form[i].name] = form[i].value
                    }
                });

                $.post(post_url, form_data, function(data) {
                    data = JSON.parse(data);
                    if (data['success'] != undefined){
                        $(form_id).trigger('reset');
                        data = data['success'];
                    } else {
                        data = data['error'];
                    }
                    Messenger().post({
                        message: data,
                        hideAfter: 4
                    });
                });
                return false;
            });
        }
     
    </script>
